India 195 is a human isolate from India and is being sequenced for a comparative genome analysis of Yersinia pestis strains from different parts of the world.~ Two libraries were constructed with average insert sizes of 1820 bp (31762 reads) and 7644 bp (24753 reads). Additional sequences from primer walk reads and PCR reactions were used to close gaps and improve quality. The assembled sequences were aligned with the finished genomic sequence of Y. pestis CO92 to predict order and orientation of contigs and scaffolds. This order and orientation is based on the assumption no major rearrangements other than the ones noted have occurred between the two genomes; however this has not been experimentally verified. Several rearrangements have been observed in India 195 relative to CO92: 1) an inversion in Chromosome_contig23, between approximate coordinates 316000 and 451500; 2) an inversion in Chromosome_contig19, between approximate coordinates 192000 and 289000; 3) a deletion of about 100 Kb has occurred in Chromosome_contig13 at approximately 158000; 4) a rearrangement in Chromosome_contig02 through Chromosome_contig07.~ Genome sequencing, assembly, and finishing were performed by the Department of Energys Joint Genome Institute (DOE-JGI), in Walnut Creek, CA and at Los Alamos National Laboratory, Los Alamos, NM. IP275 whole genome shotgun (WGS) project has the project accession AAOS00000000. This version of the project (02) has the accession number AAOS02000000, and consists of sequences AAOS02000001-AAOS02000101.; Yersinia pestis strain IP275 (original name: 17/95) was isolated in Madagascar in 1995 from a human case of bubonic plague. The patient, a 16-year-old boy from the Ambalavao district of Madagascar presented with fever, chills, and myalgia suggestive of malaria and was treated with quinine. Three days later, the appearance of a right inguinal bubo with high-grade fever (temperature of 41C), delirium, and prostration led to the diagnosis of plague. The bubo was punctured, and the patient was treated with twice-daily intramuscular injections of streptomycin (2 g per day for 4 days) and oral trimethoprim-sulfamethoxazole (2g per day for 10 days). The patient recovered but had severe asthenia for more than a month. This strain is of biovar Orientalis. Subsequent spread of plague to the rest of the western United States probably originated from this region. As such, comparisons of this strain to other North American Y. pestis strains should provide interesting insights into how Y. pestis mutated as it spread across the western United States.
